● This is a Flow Chemistry research agent project with several components
  already in place:

  - main.py — Simple entry point using PyAlex to search academic papers
  - paper_miner.py — Mines papers from academic databases
  - downloader.py — Downloads PDFs of found papers
  - paper_knowledge_extractor.py — Extracts knowledge/data from papers
  - processing.py — Processes extracted data (Suzuki reactions, etc.)

  The repo has no git commits yet and several result files already generated.

  How would you like to proceed? A few directions:

  1. Set up the repo properly — initial commit, .gitignore (to exclude API keys,
   large files, etc.), clean up structure
  2. Improve/extend existing functionality — e.g., enhance the paper miner, add
  new extraction capabilities, build a better pipeline
  3. Build something new — e.g., an AI agent that orchestrates the full workflow
   (search → download → extract → analyze)
  4. Fix/refactor — review existing code for bugs, improve error handling,
  modularize

  What's your goal with this project? That'll help me give you the best starting
   point.

❯ ok please only focus on the paper_knowledge_extractor.py agent. refer to      
details below: Context Prompt for Coding Assistant                              
Project Overview                                                                
You are helping develop FLORA (Flow Literature Oriented Retrieval Agent), a     
modular Python system that extracts structured process knowledge from chemistry 
 research PDFs. The extracted data will be used to train a RAG-based agent that 
 translates batch chemistry reactions to flow conditions, answers flow          
chemistry design questions, and defines design spaces for Bayesian              
optimization.                                                                   
                                                                                
The codebase currently implements a 5-pass PDF extraction pipeline using the    
Anthropic Claude API (claude-3-5-sonnet). Each pass has a focused, narrow job   
to maximize extraction fidelity. The final output is a structured JSON record   
per paper that will be stored in a vector database (ChromaDB or FAISS) for RAG  
retrieval.                                                                      
                                                                                
Pipeline Architecture                                                           
The 5 passes run sequentially on each PDF:                                      
                                                                                
text                                                                            
Pass 1 — Document Intelligence                                                  
         → Identifies paper structure, sections, figure/table inventory,        
           chemistry class, process mode (batch/flow/both)                      
                                                                                
Pass 2 — Chemistry Extraction                                                   
         → Reaction type, substrates, photocatalyst, co-catalyst,               
           additives, mechanism, bond formed, scope summary                     
                                                                                
Pass 3 — Quantitative Conditions Extraction                                     
         → All numerical values from text AND tables                            
         → Batch baseline + flow optimized conditions                           
         → Reactor hardware, light source, pump details                         
         → Optimization table summary (variables screened, optimal entry)       
                                                                                
Pass 4 — Figure-by-Figure Visual Extraction                                     
         → Each figure is extracted individually using image input              
         → Two-step: (1) classify figure type, (2) type-specific extraction     
         → Figure types: reactor_scheme | optimization_plot | scope_table |     
                         mechanistic_scheme | other                             
         → Each type has its own schema and prompt                              
                                                                                
Pass 5 — Synthesis and Validation                                               
         → Merges all pass outputs into one unified JSON record                 
         → Resolves conflicts between text/table/figure values                  
           (table values preferred over text for numerical fields)              
         → Cross-validates (e.g. figure shows BPR → set back_pressure to true)  
         → Computes derived fields (e.g. total flow rate = stream A + stream B) 
         → Annotates every field with _source (text/table/figure)               
           and _conf (1=inferred, 2=probable, 3=certain)                        
         → Lists remaining conflicts in a "conflicts" array                     
Key Design Decisions to Preserve                                                
Multi-pass over single-pass: Do not merge passes into one big prompt. Each pass 
 is intentionally narrow to reduce hallucination and improve accuracy.          
                                                                                
Strict null policy: Every prompt instructs the LLM to return null for missing   
fields. The LLM must never guess or infer values. This is non-negotiable for    
training data quality.                                                          
                                                                                
Table values preferred: In Pass 5, when text and table disagree on a numerical  
value, the table value wins. This must be preserved in the synthesis logic.     
                                                                                
Incremental saving: After each paper is extracted, the result is immediately    
written to disk. Never batch-save at the end — this protects against API        
failures and allows resuming interrupted runs.                                  
                                                                                
Skip already-extracted: The pipeline checks source_pdf against existing records 
 before extracting. Re-running the script on the same folder is safe and        
resumable.                                                                      
                                                                                
Figure classification before extraction: Pass 4 always runs two Claude calls    
per figure — first to classify, then to extract with the type-specific schema.  
Do not merge these into one call; classification accuracy drops significantly.  
                                                                                
Chemistry-agnostic design: Although the current test case is photochemical flow 
 reactions, the schema and prompts must stay generalizable. Do not hardcode     
photochemistry-specific logic into shared infrastructure.                       
Photochemistry-specific fields (wavelength, light power, etc.) live in their    
own sub-schema that can be swapped out.                                         
                                                                                
Current Schema Structure (Final JSON Record)                                    
text                                                                            
{                                                                               
  "chemistry": {reaction_name, reaction_class, mechanism_type,                  
                substrates, photocatalyst, co_catalyst, additives,              
                base, product, bond_formed, mechanistic_details,                
                scope_summary},                                                 
                                                                                
  "batch_baseline": {temperature_C, reaction_time_min, solvent,                 
                     concentration_M, light_source, light_power_W,              
                     atmosphere, yield_percent, ee_percent,                     
                     scale_mmol, vessel},                                       
                                                                                
  "flow_optimized": {temperature_C, residence_time_min,                         
                     flow_rate_total_mL_min, flow_rate_stream_A,                
                     flow_rate_stream_B, concentration_M,                       
                     back_pressure_bar, atmosphere, yield_percent,              
                     ee_percent, scale_mmol, throughput_mmol_h},                
                                                                                
  "optimization_table": {variables_screened, number_of_entries,                 
                         optimal_entry_number, key_findings},                   
                                                                                
  "reactor": {type, material, volume_mL, tubing_diameter_mm,                    
              channel_depth_mm},                                                
                                                                                
  "light_source": {type, wavelength_nm, power_W,                                
                   irradiance_mW_cm2, color,                                    
                   position_relative_to_reactor},                               
                                                                                
  "pump": {type, number_of_inlets},                                             
                                                                                
  "figures": [array of figure extraction results — one per figure],             
                                                                                
  "translation_logic": {batch_limitation, flow_advantage,                       
                        what_changed, what_stayed_same,                         
                        time_reduction_factor, yield_change_percent,            
                        safety_improvement, scale_up_discussed},                
                                                                                
  "process_figures": {has_reactor_scheme, has_flow_diagram,                     
                      has_optimization_table, figure_descriptions},             
                                                                                
  "field_sources": {field_name: "text|table|figure"},                           
  "field_confidence": {field_name: 1|2|3},                                      
  "conflicts": [],                                                              
  "source_pdf": "",                                                             
  "confidence_overall": 0,                                                      
  "notes": ""                                                                   
}

      311 +def _load_pdf_as_base64_pages(pdf_path: str) -> list[str]:    
      312 +    """Render each PDF page as a base64-encoded PNG for Claude

      392 +def extract_figures_with_captions(pdf_path: str) -> list[dict]
          +:                                                             
      393 +    """Extract figures + nearby caption text as paired items."
          +""                                                            
      394 +    doc = fitz.open(pdf_path)                                 
      395 +    figures = []                                              
      396 +                                                              
      397 +    for page_num, page in enumerate(doc):                     
      398 +        blocks = page.get_text("dict")["blocks"]              
      399 +                                                              
      400 +        for img in page.get_images(full=True):                
      401 +            xref = img[0]                                     
      402 +            image = doc.extract_image(xref)                   
      403 +                                                              
      404 +            # Skip logos/icons (too small)                    
      405 +            if len(image["image"]) < 15_000:                  
      406 +                continue                                      
      407 +                                                              
      408 +            caption = _find_nearby_caption(blocks)            
      409 +                                                              
      410 +            figures.append(                                   
      411 +                {                                             
      412 +                    "page": page_num + 1,                     
      413 +                    "data": image["image"],                   
      414 +                    "ext": image["ext"],                      
      415 +                    "caption": caption,                       
      416 +                }                                             
      417 +            )                                                 
      418 +                                                              
      419 +    doc.close()                                               
      420 +    return figures                                            
      421 +                                                              
      422 +                                                              
      423 +def _find_nearby_caption(blocks) -> str:                      
      424 +    """Heuristic: collect text blocks that look like figure ca
          +ptions."""                                                    
      425 +    captions = []                                             
      426 +    for block in blocks:                                      
      427 +        if block["type"] == 0:  # text block                  
      428 +            text = " ".join(                                  
      429 +                span["text"]                                  
      430 +                for line in block["lines"]                    
      431 +                for span in line["spans"]                     
      432 +            )                                                 
      433 +            if any(                                           
      434 +                text.strip().startswith(p)                    
      435 +                for p in ["Fig", "Figure", "Scheme", "Chart"] 
      436 +            ):                                                
      437 +                captions.append(text[:400])                   
      438 +    return " | ".join(captions)

      441 +def _detect_media_type(ext: str) -> str:                      
      442 +    """Map image file extension to MIME type."""              
      443 +    mapping = {"png": "image/png", "jpg": "image/jpeg", "jpeg"
          +: "image/jpeg"}                                               
      444 +    return mapping.get(ext.lower(), "image/png")

      617 +                                                              
      618 +def extract_paper(pdf_path: str, output_dir: Path = OUTPUT_DIR
          +) -> dict | None:                                             
      619 +    """Run the full 5-pass pipeline on a single PDF and save r
          +esult to disk."""                                             
      620 +    pdf_name = os.path.basename(pdf_path)                     
      621 +                                                              
      622 +    if _already_extracted(pdf_name, output_dir):              
      623 +        logger.info(f"Skipping {pdf_name} — already extracted"
          +)                                                             
      624 +        return None                                           
      625 +                                                              
      626 +    logger.info(f"Processing: {pdf_name}")                    
      627 +    start = time.time()                                       
      628 +                                                              
      629 +    # Render PDF pages once, reuse across passes 1-3          
      630 +    pages_b64 = _load_pdf_as_base64_pages(pdf_path)           
      631 +    logger.info(f"  Rendered {len(pages_b64)} pages")         
      632 +                                                              
      633 +    # --- Sequential pass execution ---                       
      634 +    pass1 = run_pass1(pages_b64)                              
      635 +    pass2 = run_pass2(pages_b64)                              
      636 +    pass3 = run_pass3(pages_b64)                              
      637 +    pass4_figures = run_pass4(pdf_path)                       
      638 +    final_record = run_pass5(pass1, pass2, pass3, pass4_figure
          +s)                                                            
      639 +                                                              
      640 +    # Attach metadata                                         
      641 +    final_record["source_pdf"] = pdf_name                     
      642 +                                                              
      643 +    # Save immediately (incremental — protects against crashes
          +)                                                             
      644 +    output_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)             
      645 +    out_path = _save_result(final_record, output_dir)         
      646 +                                                              
      647 +    elapsed = time.time() - start                             
      648 +    logger.info(f"  Done in {elapsed:.1f}s -> {out_path}")    
      649 +    return final_record                                       
      650 +                                                              
      651 +                                                              
      652 +def extract_folder(folder_path: str, output_dir: Path = OUTPUT
          +_DIR) -> list[dict]:                                          
      653 +    """Process all PDFs in a folder. Safe to re-run (skips alr
          +eady-extracted)."""                                           
      654 +    folder = Path(folder_path)                                
      655 +    pdfs = sorted(folder.glob("*.pdf"))                       
      656 +                                                              
      657 +    if not pdfs:                                              
      658 +        logger.warning(f"No PDFs found in {folder}")          
      659 +        return []                                             
      660 +                                                              
      661 +    logger.info(f"Found {len(pdfs)} PDFs in {folder}")        
      662 +    output_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)             
      663 +                                                              
      664 +    results = []                                              
      665 +    for i, pdf in enumerate(pdfs):                            
      666 +        logger.info(f"\n[{i + 1}/{len(pdfs)}] {pdf.name}")    
      667 +        try:                                                  
      668 +            result = extract_paper(str(pdf), output_dir)      
      669 +            if result:                                        
      670 +                results.append(result)                        
      671 +        except Exception as e:                                
      672 +            logger.error(f"  FAILED: {pdf.name} — {e}")       
      673 +            # Save failure record for diagnosis / resumability
      674 +            failure = {"source_pdf": pdf.name, "error": str(e)
          +, "status": "failed"}                                         
      675 +            fail_path = output_dir / f"{pdf.stem}_FAILED.json"
      676 +            fail_path.write_text(json.dumps(failure, indent=2)
          +)                                                             
      677 +                                                              
      678 +    logger.info(f"\nExtraction complete: {len(results)} papers
          + processed")                                                  
      679 +    return results

      697 +        extract_paper(target, out)                            
      698 +    elif os.path.isdir(target):                               
      699 +        extract_folder(target, out)                           
      700 +    else:                                                     
      701 +        print(f"Error: {target} is not a PDF file or directory
          +")

● The file is now a complete, working pipeline. Here's what was added on top of
  the existing prompts and figure logic:

  New infrastructure:
  - Imports & client setup — anthropic, json, logging, pathlib, etc.
  - _parse_json() — robust JSON extraction that handles markdown fences and
  partial responses
  - _load_pdf_as_base64_pages() — renders PDF pages as PNG at 200 DPI for Claude
   vision
  - _build_pdf_content_blocks() — builds multi-image + text content arrays
  - _call_claude() — centralized API call with system instruction and JSON
  parsing
  - _detect_media_type() — maps image extensions to proper MIME types

  Pass execution functions:
  - run_pass1() through run_pass5() — each calls Claude with the appropriate
  prompt
  - Pass 4 split into classify_figure() + extract_figure() (two separate API
  calls per figure, as required)
  - run_pass4() orchestrates the full figure loop with error handling per figure

  Pipeline orchestrator:
  - extract_paper() — runs all 5 passes sequentially, saves result immediately
  to disk
  - extract_folder() — processes a directory of PDFs, skips already-extracted,
  saves failure records
  - _already_extracted() — enables safe re-runs / resumption

  Key design decisions preserved:
  - Multi-pass (never merged)
  - Strict null policy in system instruction
  - Table values preferred (in Pass 5 prompt)
  - Incremental saving after each paper
  - Skip-already-extracted by checking output dir
  - Two-step figure classification before extraction
  - Chemistry-agnostic (photochemistry fields in sub-schemas only)

  Usage:
  # Single PDF
  python paper_knowledge_extractor.py paper.pdf

  # Folder of PDFs
  python paper_knowledge_extractor.py ./pdfs/ ./results/

❯ what model that data extractor is using and how much price will be consumed

● The model is set on line 38:

  MODEL = "claude-sonnet-4-20250514"

  That's Claude Sonnet 4. Let me estimate the cost per PDF.

  Pricing for Claude Sonnet 4:
  - Input: $3 / 1M tokens
  - Output: $15 / 1M tokens

  Per-PDF token estimate:

  ┌───────┬────────────────────┬─────────┬─────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Pass  │  Input (images +   │ Output  │              Notes              │
  │       │      prompt)       │         │                                 │
  ├───────┼────────────────────┼─────────┼─────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Pass  │ ~80K tokens        │ ~500    │ ~10 pages at 200 DPI (~8K       │
  │ 1     │                    │         │ tokens/page)                    │
  ├───────┼────────────────────┼─────────┼─────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Pass  │ ~80K tokens        │ ~1K     │ Same pages, different prompt    │
  │ 2     │                    │         │                                 │
  ├───────┼────────────────────┼─────────┼─────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Pass  │ ~80K tokens        │ ~2K     │ Same pages, longer output       │
  │ 3     │                    │         │                                 │
  ├───────┼────────────────────┼─────────┼─────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Pass  │ ~15K tokens x N    │ ~500 x  │ 2 calls per figure (classify +  │
  │ 4     │ figures            │ N       │ extract)                        │
  ├───────┼────────────────────┼─────────┼─────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Pass  │ ~5K tokens         │ ~3K     │ Text-only, merges all pass      │
  │ 5     │                    │         │ outputs                         │
  └───────┴────────────────────┴─────────┴─────────────────────────────────┘

  For a typical 10-page paper with 5 figures:

  ┌───────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────┬────────┐
  │               │                  Tokens                  │  Cost  │
  ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┼────────┤
  │ Input         │ ~245K + (5 figs x 2 calls x 15K) = ~395K │ ~$1.19 │
  ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┼────────┤
  │ Output        │ ~3.5K + (5 figs x 2 x 500) = ~8.5K       │ ~$0.13 │
  ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┼────────┤
  │ Total per PDF │                                          │ ~$1.30 │
  └───────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────┴────────┘

  Rough ranges:
  - Short paper (5 pages, 2 figures): ~$0.70
  - Typical paper (10 pages, 5 figures): ~$1.30
  - Long paper (20 pages, 10 figures): ~$2.50

  The biggest cost driver is sending the full PDF images 3 times (passes 1-3
  each get all pages). The pages are rendered at 200 DPI, which is high-fidelity
   but token-heavy.

  Cost reduction options if needed:
  1. Drop DPI to 150 — cuts image tokens ~40%, minor quality loss on tables
  2. Switch to claude-haiku-4-5 — ~10x cheaper ($0.80/$4 per 1M), but lower
  extraction accuracy
  3. Use Sonnet for passes 3-5, Haiku for passes 1-2 — hybrid approach, ~50%
  savings
  4. Cache pages — enable prompt caching so passes 1-3 share the cached image
  tokens (reduces input cost by ~60% for the repeated pages)

  Want me to implement prompt caching or a hybrid model strategy?

❯ do whatever it takes to reduce the cost while keeping the quality of          
extracting also high                                                            

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

      728 +                                                              
      729 +                                                              
      730 +def extract_folder_batch(                                     
      731 +    folder_path: str, output_dir: Path = OUTPUT_DIR           
      732 +) -> str:                                                     
      733 +    """Submit all PDFs as a Batch API job (50% cheaper, async)
          +.                                                             
      734 +                                                              
      735 +    Returns the batch ID. Use `poll_batch()` to check status a
          +nd                                                            
      736 +    download results.                                         
      737 +    """                                                       
      738 +    folder = Path(folder_path)                                
      739 +    pdfs = sorted(folder.glob("*.pdf"))                       
      740 +    output_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)             
      741 +                                                              
      742 +    requests = []                                             
      743 +    for pdf in pdfs:                                          
      744 +        pdf_name = pdf.name                                   
      745 +        if _already_extracted(pdf_name, output_dir):          
      746 +            logger.info(f"Skipping {pdf_name} — already extrac
          +ted")                                                         
      747 +            continue                                          
      748 +                                                              
      749 +        pdf_text = _extract_pdf_text(str(pdf))                
      750 +        pages_b64 = _load_pdf_as_base64_pages(str(pdf))       
      751 +        stem = pdf.stem                                       
      752 +                                                              
      753 +        # Pass 1 — text                                       
      754 +        content1 = [{"type": "text", "text": pdf_text + "\n\n"
          + + PASS1_PROMPT}]                                             
      755 +        requests.append(_build_batch_request(f"{stem}__pass1",
          + content1, 1024))                                             
      756 +                                                              
      757 +        # Pass 2 — text                                       
      758 +        content2 = [{"type": "text", "text": pdf_text + "\n\n"
          + + PASS2_PROMPT}]                                             
      759 +        requests.append(_build_batch_request(f"{stem}__pass2",
          + content2, 2048))                                             
      760 +                                                              
      761 +        # Pass 3 — vision                                     
      762 +        content3 = _build_vision_content(pages_b64, PASS3_PROM
          +PT)                                                           
      763 +        requests.append(_build_batch_request(f"{stem}__pass3",
          + content3, 4096))                                             
      764 +                                                              
      765 +    if not requests:                                          
      766 +        logger.info("No new PDFs to process")                 
      767 +        return ""                                             
      768 +                                                              
      769 +    logger.info(f"Submitting batch with {len(requests)} reques
          +ts")                                                          
      770 +    batch = client.messages.batches.create(requests=requests) 
      771 +    logger.info(f"Batch submitted: {batch.id}")               
      772 +    return batch.id                                           
      773 +                                                              
      774 +                                                              
      775 +def poll_batch(batch_id: str) -> dict:                        
      776 +    """Check batch status. Returns the batch object."""       
      777 +    batch = client.messages.batches.retrieve(batch_id)        
      778 +    logger.info(                                              
      779 +        f"Batch {batch_id}: status={batch.processing_status}, 
          +"                                                             
      780 +        f"succeeded={batch.request_counts.succeeded}, "       
      781 +        f"failed={batch.request_counts.errored}"              
      782 +    )                                                         
      783 +    return batch                                              
      784 +                                                              
      785 +                                                              
      786 +# ------------------------------------------------------------
          +---------------                                               
      787 +# Standard folder processing (synchronous, real-time)         
      788 +# ------------------------------------------------------------
          +---------------                                               
      789 +                                                              
      790 +                                                              
      791  def extract_folder(folder_path: str, output_dir: Path = OUTPUT
           _DIR) -> list[dict]:
      792      """Process all PDFs in a folder. Safe to re-run (skips alr
           eady-extracted)."""
      793      folder = Path(folder_path)
     ...
      809                  results.append(result)
      810          except Exception as e:
      811              logger.error(f"  FAILED: {pdf.name} — {e}")
      672 -            # Save failure record for diagnosis / resumability

      814              fail_path.write_text(json.dumps(failure, indent=2)

● Here's the updated cost breakdown for a typical 10-page paper with 5 figures 
  (2 "other"):

  Before vs After

  ┌─────────────────────────┬──────────────────┬───────────────┬────────────┐
  │                         │      Before      │     After     │  Savings   │
  ├─────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────┤
  │ Pass 1 (text vs vision) │ ~80K img tokens  │ ~8K text =    │ 90%        │
  │                         │ = $0.24          │ $0.024        │            │
  ├─────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────┤
  │ Pass 2 (text vs vision) │ ~80K img tokens  │ ~8K text =    │ 90%        │
  │                         │ = $0.24          │ $0.024        │            │
  ├─────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────┤
  │ Pass 3 (150 vs 200 DPI) │ ~80K tokens =    │ ~50K tokens = │ 37%        │
  │                         │ $0.24            │  $0.15        │            │
  ├─────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────┤
  │ Pass 4 classify (Haiku  │ 5 x Sonnet =     │ 5 x Haiku =   │ 91%        │
  │ vs Sonnet)              │ $0.23            │ $0.02         │            │
  ├─────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────┤
  │ Pass 4 extract (skip    │ 5 x Sonnet =     │ 3 x Sonnet =  │ 39%        │
  │ "other")                │ $0.23            │ $0.14         │            │
  ├─────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────┤
  │ Pass 5                  │ $0.06            │ $0.06         │ —          │
  ├─────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼───────────────┼────────────┤
  │ Total per PDF           │ ~$1.30           │ ~$0.42        │ ~68%       │
  │                         │                  │               │ cheaper    │
  └─────────────────────────┴──────────────────┴───────────────┴────────────┘

  With Batch API (folder processing)

  --batch mode uses Anthropic's Batch API for an additional 50% off, bringing it
   to ~$0.21/paper.

  What changed:

  1. Passes 1-2 use extracted text — PyMuPDF text extraction, no images sent
  2. Pass 3 renders at 150 DPI instead of 200 (still reads tables accurately)
  3. Haiku classifies figures in Pass 4 (trivial task, 10x cheaper)
  4. "Other" figures skip extraction — no Sonnet call for decorative/irrelevant
  figures
  5. Prompt caching on system instructions and image blocks
  6. Batch API option for folder processing (--batch flag, 50% discount)

  Usage:

  # Real-time (single PDF or folder)
  python paper_knowledge_extractor.py paper.pdf
  python paper_knowledge_extractor.py ./pdfs/

  # Batch mode — 50% cheaper, async
  python paper_knowledge_extractor.py --batch ./pdfs/
  python paper_knowledge_extractor.py --poll batch_abc123

❯ how can i see how much so far from the API for this pdf project has been      
consumed or costed?                                                             

● Two ways:

  1. Anthropic Console (historical usage)

  Go to console.anthropic.com → Usage → filter by date range. This shows all API
   calls billed to your key.

  2. Add cost tracking to FLORA itself

  The API response already includes token counts — we just need to capture them.
   Let me add a built-in cost tracker:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Now I have the full picture. I'll add a CostTracker class and wire it into
  _call_claude so every API call is tracked, then print a summary after each
  paper and persist a cost log.

       58 +    MODEL: {"input": 3.00, "output": 15.00, "cache_read": 0.30
          +, "cache_write": 3.75},                                       
       59 +    MODEL_CHEAP: {"input": 0.80, "output": 4.00, "cache_read":
          + 0.08, "cache_write": 1.00},                                  
       60 +}                                                             
       61 +                                                              
       62  logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO, format=LOG_FORMAT)
       63  logger = logging.getLogger("flora")
       64  
       65  client = anthropic.Anthropic()  # reads ANTHROPIC_API_KEY from
            env
       66  
       67 +                                                              
       68  # ------------------------------------------------------------
           ---------------
       69 +# Cost Tracker                                                
       70 +# ------------------------------------------------------------
          +---------------                                               
       71 +                                                              
       72 +                                                              
       73 +@dataclass                                                    
       74 +class CostTracker:                                            
       75 +    """Tracks token usage and cost across all API calls in a s
          +ession."""                                                    
       76 +                                                              
       77 +    calls: list[dict] = field(default_factory=list)           
       78 +                                                              
       79 +    def record(self, model: str, usage, label: str = "") -> fl
          +oat:                                                          
       80 +        """Record a single API call's usage. Returns the cost 
          +of this call."""                                              
       81 +        prices = PRICING.get(model, PRICING[MODEL])           
       82 +        input_tokens = getattr(usage, "input_tokens", 0)      
       83 +        output_tokens = getattr(usage, "output_tokens", 0)    
       84 +        cache_read = getattr(usage, "cache_read_input_tokens",
          + 0) or 0                                                      
       85 +        cache_write = getattr(usage, "cache_creation_input_tok
          +ens", 0) or 0                                                 
       86 +                                                              
       87 +        cost = (                                              
       88 +            (input_tokens / 1_000_000) * prices["input"]      
       89 +            + (output_tokens / 1_000_000) * prices["output"]  
       90 +            + (cache_read / 1_000_000) * prices["cache_read"] 
       91 +            + (cache_write / 1_000_000) * prices["cache_write"
          +]                                                             
       92 +        )                                                     
       93 +                                                              
       94 +        entry = {                                             
       95 +            "label": label,                                   
       96 +            "model": model,                                   
       97 +            "input_tokens": input_tokens,                     
       98 +            "output_tokens": output_tokens,                   
       99 +            "cache_read_tokens": cache_read,                  
      100 +            "cache_write_tokens": cache_write,                
      101 +            "cost_usd": round(cost, 6),                       
      102 +            "timestamp": time.strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"),  
      103 +        }                                                     
      104 +        self.calls.append(entry)                              
      105 +        return cost                                           
      106 +                                                              
      107 +    @property                                                 
      108 +    def total_cost(self) -> float:                            
      109 +        return sum(c["cost_usd"] for c in self.calls)         
      110 +                                                              
      111 +    @property                                                 
      112 +    def total_input(self) -> int:                             
      113 +        return sum(c["input_tokens"] for c in self.calls)     
      114 +                                                              
      115 +    @property                                                 
      116 +    def total_output(self) -> int:                            
      117 +        return sum(c["output_tokens"] for c in self.calls)    
      118 +                                                              
      119 +    def summary(self, label: str = "") -> str:                
      120 +        """Human-readable cost summary."""                    
      121 +        if label:                                             
      122 +            calls = [c for c in self.calls if c["label"].start
          +swith(label)]                                                 
      123 +        else:                                                 
      124 +            calls = self.calls                                
      125 +        total = sum(c["cost_usd"] for c in calls)             
      126 +        inp = sum(c["input_tokens"] for c in calls)           
      127 +        out = sum(c["output_tokens"] for c in calls)          
      128 +        cr = sum(c["cache_read_tokens"] for c in calls)       
      129 +        cw = sum(c["cache_write_tokens"] for c in calls)      
      130 +        n = len(calls)                                        
      131 +        lines = [                                             
      132 +            f"{'[' + label + '] ' if label else ''}Cost Summar
          +y:",                                                          
      133 +            f"  API calls:        {n}",                       
      134 +            f"  Input tokens:     {inp:,}",                   
      135 +            f"  Output tokens:    {out:,}",                   
      136 +            f"  Cache read:       {cr:,}",                    
      137 +            f"  Cache write:      {cw:,}",                    
      138 +            f"  Total cost:       ${total:.4f}",              
      139 +        ]                                                     
      140 +        return "\n".join(lines)                               
      141 +                                                              
      142 +    def save(self, path: Path = COST_LOG) -> None:            
      143 +        """Append session costs to a persistent JSON log file.
          +"""                                                           
      144 +        path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)        
      145 +        existing = []                                         
      146 +        if path.exists():                                     
      147 +            try:                                              
      148 +                existing = json.loads(path.read_text())       
      149 +            except (json.JSONDecodeError, ValueError):        
      150 +                existing = []                                 
      151 +        existing.extend(self.calls)                           
      152 +        path.write_text(json.dumps(existing, indent=2))       
      153 +                                                              
      154 +                                                              
      155 +# Global tracker for the current session                      
      156 +tracker = CostTracker()                                       
      157 +                                                              
      158 +# ------------------------------------------------------------
          +---------------                                               
      159  # System instructions (cacheable — shared prefix across all ca
           lls)
      160  # ------------------------------------------------------------
           ---------------

FLORA-Translate: Complete Implementation Guideline                              
For coding agent — chemistry context + full technical specification             
Version 1.0 | March 2026                                                        
=============================================================================== 
=                                                                               
                                                                                
SECTION 0 — WHAT THIS MODULE DOES (READ FIRST)                                  
FLORA-Translate takes a batch chemistry protocol as input and returns a         
                                                                                
physically validated, literature-grounded flow chemistry design as output.      
It does NOT invent a flow design. It finds the most similar batch-to-flow       
                                                                                
translation examples in your corpus of 140 JSON records, uses them as           
                                                                                
analogies, and has an LLM synthesize a flow proposal based on those analogies.  
                                                                                
An engineering validation layer (ENGINE) then checks the proposal for physical  
                                                                                
and hardware feasibility before returning it to the user.                       
INPUT:  A batch protocol (text or structured)                                   
                                                                                
OUTPUT: A validated flow design (structured JSON + human-readable explanation)  
=============================================================================== 
=                                                                               
                                                                                
SECTION 1 — CHEMISTRY DOMAIN KNOWLEDGE FOR THE CODING AGENT                     
1.1 WHY BATCH AND FLOW CONDITIONS DIFFER                                        
When a chemist moves a reaction from batch to flow, the following parameters    
                                                                                
change systematically. The coding agent must understand these so the LLM        
                                                                                
prompts are correctly framed.                                                   
Parameter    Batch typical value    Flow typical value                          
Reaction time    1–24 hours    1–60 minutes (residence time)                    
Temperature    Often room temp or    Can be higher (better heat transfer        
reflux    allows faster kinetics)                                               
Concentration    0.1–1.0 M    0.05–0.5 M (often diluted slightly                
    to avoid clogging or fouling)                                               
Scale    mmol–gram scale    Continuous (scale by time, not volume)              
Mixing    Magnetic stir bar    T-mixer, Y-mixer, static mixer                   
Reactor    Round-bottom flask    Coil (FEP/PFA/SS tubing), chip, column         
Pressure    Atmospheric (1 bar)    2–20 bar (back-pressure                      
… +1226 lines …                                                                 
    # Claude API                                                                
                                                                                
chromadb>=0.5.0          # vector database                                      
                                                                                
pydantic>=2.0.0          # data schemas                                         
                                                                                
pint>=0.23               # unit handling and physics calculations               
                                                                                
numpy>=1.24.0                                                                   
                                                                                
pandas>=2.0.0                                                                   
                                                                                
python-dotenv            # API key management                                   
                                                                                
fastapi + uvicorn        # if building web API                                  
Environment variables (.env):                                                   
                                                                                
OPENAI_API_KEY=...                                                              
                                                                                
ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=...                                                           
=============================================================================== 
=                                                                               
                                                                                
SECTION 12 — EVALUATION HOOKS (for manuscript)                                  
def evaluate_translation(                                                       
                                                                                
batch_record: BatchRecord,                                                      
                                                                                
predicted: FlowProposal,                                                        
                                                                                
ground_truth: ConditionsRecord                                                  
                                                                                
) -> dict:                                                                      
                                                                                
"""Compute evaluation metrics for one test case."""                             
                                                                                
metrics = {}                                                                    
Numerical MAPE                                                                  
for field in ["residence_time_min", "temperature_C",                            
                                                                                
"flow_rate_mL_min", "concentration_M"]:                                         
                                                                                
pred = getattr(predicted, field, None)                                          
                                                                                
true = getattr(ground_truth, field, None)                                       
                                                                                
if pred and true:                                                               
                                                                                
metrics[f"MAPE_{field}"] = abs(pred - true) / true * 100                        
Categorical match                                                               
for field in ["reactor_type", "tubing_material", "BPR_required"]:               
                                                                                
pred = getattr(predicted, field, None)                                          
                                                                                
true = getattr(ground_truth, field, None)                                       
                                                                                
metrics[f"match_{field}"] = int(pred == true)                                   
return metrics                                                                  
def llm_judge(batch_record, proposal, ground_truth) -> dict:                    
                                                                                
"""LLM-as-judge scoring on chemical validity and literature alignment."""       
Prompt Claude to score 1-5 on:                                                  
- chemical_validity: is the proposal chemically sensible?                       
- literature_alignment: does it match the ground truth conditions?              
- physical_feasibility: are the engineering parameters realistic?               
pass                                                                            
=============================================================================== 
=                                                                               
                                                                                
SECTION 13 — KNOWN LIMITATIONS TO DOCUMENT                                      
1.    Records without translation_record.batch_baseline cannot be used as       
direct                                                                          
                                                                                
analogies — they are silently filtered before retrieval.                        
2.    Solvent viscosity lookup covers ~15 common solvents. Unknown solvents     
default                                                                         
                                                                                
to η = 1.0 cP with a warning flag.                                              
3.    Intensification factor estimation is empirical. The Kinetics Agent does   
not                                                                             
                                                                                
model reaction kinetics from first principles — it uses literature priors.      
4.    P&ID generation is text-based only in v1. Visual diagram rendering is v2. 
5.    The evaluation requires ground truth batch-to-flow pairs. For novel       
reactions                                                                       
                                                                                
with no literature analogy (similarity score < 0.5), confidence = LOW and       
                                                                                
the output should be treated as a hypothesis only.                              
=============================================================================== 
=                                                                               
                                                                                
END OF GUIDELINE

  streamlit run app.py

❯ now if i run the app.py it is done?                                           

● Almost — you need two things before it works end-to-end:

  1. Set your API keys

  export ANTHROPIC_API_KEY="your-key-here"
  export OPENAI_API_KEY="your-key-here"    # needed for embeddings

  2. Index your extracted papers

  You need extraction results in extraction_results/ first (from
  paper_knowledge_extractor.py), then index them:

  # Copy extraction results to the records folder
  cp extraction_results/*.json flora_translate/data/records/

  # Index into ChromaDB
  python -m flora_translate.main index flora_translate/data/records/

  3. Then launch

  streamlit run app.py

  If you don't have extracted papers yet, the app will still launch — you can
  browse the GUI, but FLORA-Translate won't find any analogies (it'll return LOW
   confidence results based on general chemistry knowledge only).

  The minimum working flow is:
  1. Extract papers: python paper_knowledge_extractor.py pdfs/
  2. Index them: python -m flora_translate.main index extraction_results/
  3. Run the GUI: streamlit run app.py

  Want me to run it now, or do you want to extract some papers first?

❯ what is happening during indexing?                                            

● During indexing, each extracted JSON record goes through 3 steps:

  Step 1 — Normalize the extraction record

  vector_store.py:_normalize_extraction_record()

  Your extractor outputs this schema:
  {"chemistry": {...}, "batch_baseline": {...}, "flow_optimized": {...},
  "reactor": {...}}

  Indexing maps it into the FLORA-Translate schema (ProcessRecord):
  - Detects process_mode (batch/flow/both) by checking if both batch_baseline
  and flow_optimized have yield values
  - Builds a TranslationRecord with the batch→flow pair (these are the gold 
  pairs used for retrieval)
  - Maps reactor, pump, light source fields into ProcessDesignRecord

  Step 2 — Generate embedding summary

  embedding_engine.py:generate_record_summary()

  Sends the full JSON record to Claude with this instruction:

  ▎ "Summarize this flow chemistry process record in 4-6 sentences... Include 
  reaction type, photocatalyst, key conditions, reactor type, and why flow 
  improved on batch."

  This produces something like:
  ▎ "Ir(ppy)3-photocatalyzed [2+2] cycloaddition of styrene derivatives in MeCN 
  at 25°C. Flow residence time of 10 min replaced 24h batch reaction using FEP 
  coil reactor (1.0mm ID, 5mL) with 450nm blue LED. Yield improved from 78% to 
  92%..."

  Raw JSON is not embedded directly — natural language summaries give much
  better semantic search results.

  Step 3 — Embed and store in ChromaDB

  embedding_engine.py:embed() → vector_store.py:index_record()

  - Sends the summary to OpenAI text-embedding-3-small → gets a 1536-dim vector
  - Stores in two ChromaDB collections:
    - flora_records — all records
    - flora_pairs — only records where has_translation=True (both batch AND flow
   data exist)

  Each record is stored with filterable metadata:
  photocatalyst, wavelength_nm, solvent, reactor_type,
  chemistry_class, confidence, has_translation, doi, year

  Cost per record

  - 1 Claude call (summary generation): ~$0.01
  - 1 OpenAI embedding call: ~$0.00002
  - ~$0.01 per record, so ~$1.40 for 140 papers

  Why this matters

  When you later query "translate this batch protocol", the retriever:
  1. Embeds your query the same way
  2. Searches flora_pairs collection (semantic similarity)
  3. Reranks by field matching (catalyst class, solvent, wavelength)
  4. Returns the top-3 most similar batch→flow translations as analogies

  Without indexing, there's nothing to search against.

❯ so now i asked the agent:direct S-alkylation of sulfenamides to produce       
sulfilimines, which are key intermediates for high-value sulfoximines.          
(photochemical reaction). the agent gave me some results with some process etc. 
 but seems like the agent does not know the chemistry. it says: " pump 1 has    
reagent 1" pump 2 has reagent 2. it means this agent does not understands       
chemistry what are the reactants and what are the chemical stuff. Am i correct? 

● You're absolutely correct. Right now the agent is essentially a hardware 
  parameter matcher — it knows flow rates, tubing, BPR, residence times — but it
   treats the chemistry as a black box. Specifically:

  What's missing:
  1. Stream assignment — It says "Pump A (reagent 1)" instead of "Pump A:
  sulfenamide (0.1M in MeCN) + photocatalyst" and "Pump B: alkylating agent (1.5
   equiv)"
  2. Reagent-to-stream logic — It doesn't reason about why certain reagents go
  in separate streams (e.g., premixing could cause dark reaction, or an oxidant
  must be added downstream)
  3. Mechanism-aware design — For your photochemical sulfilimime synthesis, it
  should know that the photocatalyst needs to be pre-dissolved with the
  substrate, deoxygenation matters, and the nitrene/radical intermediate
  dictates mixing order

  Let me fix this by adding chemistry awareness to the translation prompt and
  Process Architect.

  Read 3 files (ctrl+o to expand)

  1. Add chemistry-aware fields to FlowProposal (stream assignments, reagent
  details)
  2. Rewrite the translation prompt to require chemistry reasoning and stream
  assignments
  3. Make Process Architect use LLM to generate chemistry-aware unit operations
  instead of hardcoded generic ones

❯ how this chemistry is being decided? do not code let's talk now               

● The chemistry understanding comes from two sources, and both have limitations:

  Source 1 — Literature analogies (RAG retrieval)

  When you query "S-alkylation of sulfenamides, photochemical", the system:
  1. Searches ChromaDB for similar papers
  2. Returns the top-3 batch→flow translation pairs
  3. Feeds those as examples to Claude

  So if your corpus has a paper on photochemical sulfenamide chemistry, Claude
  sees that paper's specific reagents, streams, and conditions. But if no close
  match exists, it's flying blind.

  Source 2 — Claude's general chemistry knowledge

  The translation LLM (Claude Sonnet) does inherently know organic chemistry.
  When the prompt now says "name every reagent, assign to streams, explain why",
   Claude uses its training knowledge to reason about the mechanism.

  So the chemistry reasoning is essentially Claude's built-in knowledge, guided 
  by literature analogies when available.

  The honest limitation

  This is not a computational chemistry engine. It doesn't:
  - Compute reaction energetics
  - Verify that a proposed mechanism is feasible
  - Know if a specific substrate will actually work
  - Model kinetics from first principles

  It's an analogy machine — "this similar reaction worked in flow with these
  conditions, so yours probably will too" — plus Claude's general chemistry
  sense for stream assignment and mechanism reasoning.

  Where it works well

  - Reactions with close literature precedent (your corpus has similar
  chemistry)
  - Standard photocatalyst systems (Ir, Ru, organic) where Claude knows the
  mechanism

  Where it's weak

  - Novel chemistry with no analogy in the corpus (confidence = LOW, and rightly
   so)
  - Complex multi-step sequences where stream timing matters
  - Heterogeneous reactions, gas-liquid systems, or non-standard setups

  The quality is directly proportional to your corpus quality. With 140
  well-extracted photochemistry papers, it should do well for common
  photocatalytic transformations. For your sulfilimines case — if there's no
  sulfenamide paper in the corpus, it's relying purely on Claude's general
  knowledge plus whatever the closest photochemical analogy looks like.

  Does this match what you observed? And do you want to push the chemistry
  reasoning further in a specific direction?

❯ i want to make it further more deep into chemistry. how we can do it?         

● Good question. Let me think about this architecturally, not just code.

  The core problem

  Right now the chemistry "understanding" is a single LLM call that
  simultaneously picks hardware AND reasons about chemistry. That's asking one
  prompt to do too much — the chemistry reasoning gets diluted by hardware
  decisions.

  How to go deeper — three layers

  Layer 1 — Chemistry Reasoning Agent (new, runs BEFORE hardware)

  A dedicated Claude call that ONLY thinks about chemistry:
  - Identifies the reaction mechanism (radical, ionic, energy transfer, HAT,
  etc.)
  - Maps every species: substrate, reagent, catalyst, sensitizer, oxidant, base,
   quencher
  - Determines which species interact and in what order
  - Decides stream separation logic based on mechanism (e.g., "the nitrene
  precursor must not contact the photocatalyst in the dark because SET would
  decompose it")
  - Identifies oxygen sensitivity, moisture sensitivity, light sensitivity
  - Specifies quench requirements based on what reactive intermediates remain

  This agent outputs a ChemistryPlan — no hardware, purely chemical logic.

  Layer 2 — Translation LLM (existing, but now receives ChemistryPlan)

  Takes the ChemistryPlan + analogies and maps it to hardware. Now it's not
  guessing the chemistry — it's translating a chemistry plan into engineering
  parameters.

  Layer 3 — Chemistry Validator (new, runs in ENGINE council)

  A new council agent that checks the proposal AGAINST the ChemistryPlan:
  - Does the wavelength match the photocatalyst absorption?
  - Is the concentration reasonable for this mechanism (e.g., radical chain
  reactions need higher concentration)?
  - Is the stoichiometry between streams correct?
  - Does the residence time make sense for this reaction type?
  - Are incompatible reagents actually in separate streams?

  What this changes in the pipeline

  Current:
    BatchRecord → Retrieve → LLM (chemistry + hardware) → ENGINE → Output

  Proposed:
    BatchRecord → ChemistryAgent → ChemistryPlan
                                         ↓
                                Retrieve (better: plan-aware query)
                                         ↓
                                TranslationLLM (plan + analogies → hardware)
                                         ↓
                                ENGINE + ChemistryValidator
                                         ↓
                                      Output

  The second big win — plan-aware retrieval

  Right now retrieval searches based on the raw batch description. But if the
  ChemistryAgent first identifies "this is a SET-mediated nitrene insertion via
  Ir(III) photocatalysis", the retrieval query becomes much more specific. It
  can search for SET nitrene mechanisms, not just "sulfenamide reactions".

  What this does NOT solve

  - If the chemistry is truly novel (no analogues at all), no amount of
  architecture helps — you need experimental data
  - Claude can still hallucinate mechanisms — the ChemistryValidator helps catch
   this but isn't perfect
  - Quantitative predictions (exact yield, exact optimal residence time) remain
  empirical

  The question for you

  How far do you want to go? Options:

  1. Just add the Chemistry Reasoning Agent — biggest impact, adds the
  ChemistryPlan step before translation. Medium effort.
  2. Agent + plan-aware retrieval — also improves analogy selection. Larger
  change.
  3. Full three-layer — Agent + better retrieval + Chemistry Validator in ENGINE
   council. Full rewrite of the pipeline flow.

  Which direction?

❯ direction 3. please go on

      204              )

      207 +                                                              
      208 +    def _build_plan_aware_query(                              
      209 +        self, batch_record: BatchRecord, plan: ChemistryPlan  
      210 +    ) -> str:                                                 
      211 +        """Build a retrieval query enriched with chemistry pla
          +n insights.                                                   
      212 +                                                              
      213 +        Instead of just describing the batch protocol, this qu
          +ery includes                                                  
      214 +        mechanism type, reaction class, key intermediate, and 
          +retrieval                                                     
      215 +        keywords — making semantic search much more targeted. 
      216 +        """                                                   
      217 +        parts = []                                            
      218 +                                                              
      219 +        # Reaction identity from plan (more specific than raw 
          +batch description)                                            
      220 +        if plan.reaction_name:                                
      221 +            parts.append(f"{plan.reaction_name}.")            
      222 +        if plan.reaction_class:                               
      223 +            parts.append(f"Reaction class: {plan.reaction_clas
          +s}.")                                                         
      224 +        if plan.mechanism_type:                               
      225 +            parts.append(f"Mechanism: {plan.mechanism_type}.")
      226 +                                                              
      227 +        # Key species                                         
      228 +        catalyst_names = [                                    
      229 +            r.name for r in plan.reagents                     
      230 +            if r.role in ("photocatalyst", "sensitizer", "co-c
          +atalyst") and r.name                                          
      231 +        ]                                                     
      232 +        if catalyst_names:                                    
      233 +            parts.append(f"Photocatalyst: {', '.join(catalyst_
          +names)}.")                                                    
      234 +                                                              
      235 +        # Conditions from batch record                        
      236 +        if batch_record.solvent:                              
      237 +            parts.append(f"Solvent: {batch_record.solvent}.") 
      238 +        if batch_record.temperature_C is not None:            
      239 +            parts.append(f"Temperature: {batch_record.temperat
          +ure_C}°C.")                                                   
      240 +        if batch_record.wavelength_nm:                        
      241 +            parts.append(f"Wavelength: {batch_record.wavelengt
          +h_nm} nm.")                                                   
      242 +        elif plan.recommended_wavelength_nm:                  
      243 +            parts.append(f"Wavelength: {plan.recommended_wavel
          +ength_nm} nm.")                                               
      244 +                                                              
      245 +        # Key intermediate and bond formed (highly discriminat
          +ive)                                                          
      246 +        if plan.key_intermediate:                             
      247 +            parts.append(f"Key intermediate: {plan.key_interme
          +diate}.")                                                     
      248 +        if plan.bond_formed:                                  
      249 +            parts.append(f"Bond formed: {plan.bond_formed}.") 
      250 +                                                              
      251 +        # Retrieval keywords from chemistry agent             
      252 +        if plan.retrieval_keywords:                           
      253 +            parts.append(f"Keywords: {', '.join(plan.retrieval
          +_keywords[:6])}.")                                            
      254 +                                                              
      255 +        # Similar reaction classes                            
      256 +        if plan.similar_reaction_classes:                     
      257 +            parts.append(                                     
      258 +                f"Similar reactions: {', '.join(plan.similar_r
          +eaction_classes[:4])}."                                       
      259 +            )                                                 
      260 +                                                              
      261 +        # Flow-relevant notes                                 
      262 +        if plan.oxygen_sensitive:                             
      263 +            parts.append("Oxygen-sensitive reaction requiring 
          +deoxygenation.")                                              
      264 +                                                              
      265 +        return " ".join(parts)

● All three layers work. The validator correctly caught all three deliberate
  errors in the test:

  1. Wrong wavelength (530nm vs 450nm needed) → REJECT
  2. Incompatible pair in same stream (sulfenamide + NCS together) → REJECT
  3. Missing deoxygenation for O2-sensitive reaction → REJECT

  Here's the new pipeline architecture:

  BatchRecord
       │
       ▼
  [1] ChemistryReasoningAgent (NEW — Layer 1)
       │  → Identifies all species + roles
       │  → Proposes mechanism step-by-step
       │  → Determines stream separation logic
       │  → Flags sensitivities (O2, moisture, light)
       │  → Generates retrieval keywords
       │  → Outputs: ChemistryPlan
       │
       ▼
  [2] VectorRetriever (IMPROVED — plan-aware query)
       │  → Uses mechanism type, key intermediate, catalyst class,
       │    retrieval keywords for much better semantic search
       │
       ▼
  [3] TranslationLLM (IMPROVED — receives ChemistryPlan)
       │  → Chemistry Plan is AUTHORITATIVE for stream assignments
       │  → Analogies are AUTHORITATIVE for hardware parameters
       │  → Outputs: FlowProposal
       │
       ▼
  [4] ENGINE Council (EXPANDED — 5 agents now)
       │  ├── ChemistryValidator (NEW — Layer 3)
       │  │     → Wavelength vs photocatalyst match
       │  │     → Incompatible pairs not in same stream
       │  │     → Deoxygenation present if O2-sensitive
       │  │     → Quench present if needed
       │  │     → All planned reagents accounted for
       │  │     → Concentration sanity for mechanism type
       │  │     → Light-sensitive reagent warnings
       │  ├── KineticsAgent
       │  ├── FluidicsAgent
       │  └── SafetyCriticAgent
       │
       ▼
  [5] ProcessArchitect + OutputFormatter
       → Chemistry-aware unit operations
       → Human-readable explanation

  - flora_translate/engine/chemistry_validator.py — Layer 3 (7 chemistry checks)

❯ how can i make the streamlit available online that my collaborator also see   
it                                                                              

● Several options, from easiest to most robust:

  Option 1 — Streamlit Community Cloud (free, easiest)

  Push your code to a public GitHub repo, then deploy at share.streamlit.io:

  1. Create a requirements.txt
  2. Push to GitHub
  3. Connect at share.streamlit.io → pick the repo → deploy

  Caveats: your API keys go in Streamlit's "Secrets" manager (not in code), and
  the repo must be public (or you need a paid plan for private).

  Option 2 — ngrok (quickest for right now, temporary)

  Exposes your local machine to the internet with one command:

  # Install ngrok
  pip install pyngrok

  # Run your app
  streamlit run app.py --server.port 8501 &

  # Expose it
  ngrok http 8501

  You get a URL like https://abc123.ngrok-free.app — share it with your
  collaborator. Stops when you close your terminal.

  Option 3 — Hugging Face Spaces (free, persistent)

  Similar to Streamlit Cloud but on HF infrastructure. Create a Space, push your
   code, it runs.

  ---
  Which one do you want? If you just need your collaborator to see it today, I'd
   go with Option 2 (ngrok) — takes 30 seconds. If you want it permanently
  available, Option 1 (Streamlit Cloud) is the standard choice.

❯ tell me the ngrok way again (do not code just guide me)                       

● ngrok — Quick Guide

  Step 1: Sign up at ngrok.com and get your auth token (free tier is fine).

  Step 2: Install ngrok:
  pip install pyngrok

  Step 3: Authenticate once:
  ngrok config add-authtoken YOUR_TOKEN_HERE

  Step 4: Start your Streamlit app:
  streamlit run app.py

  Step 5: In a separate terminal, expose it:
  ngrok http 8501

  Step 6: ngrok prints a public URL like:
  Forwarding  https://a1b2c3d4.ngrok-free.app → http://localhost:8501

  Send that URL to your collaborator. They open it in any browser — no install
  needed.

  Things to know

  - Stops when you close the terminal or hit Ctrl+C
  - Free tier gives a random URL that changes each time you restart ngrok
  - Your machine must stay on — it's tunneling to your localhost
  - API keys stay on your machine — your collaborator never sees them
  - First-time visitors see an ngrok interstitial page ("Visit Site") — that's
  normal on the free tier
